Here's what I found:

---

## Session Persistence (Good News)

**Sessions are automatically saved continuously.** If you close the terminal by accident:
- The conversation up to that point is preserved on disk
- Sessions are stored in `~/.claude/projects/`
- Resume with `claude --continue` (most recent) or `claude --resume` (picker)
- Checkpoints are created at every user prompt

**Your logs won't be lost.** The only thing that wouldn't run is the SessionEnd hook (since the session didn't end cleanly). But the transcript itself is saved.

---

## Blot Integration

Based on research, Blot offers:
- **Git sync** - Push to `https://blot.im/clients/git/end/[your-folder].git`
- **Dropbox/Google Drive sync** - Folder-based

**Subdirectory limitation:** Blot appears to sync the **entire repository**, not a subdirectory. There's no documented way to point Blot at `Anchor/website/` within a larger repo.

**Options:**

1. **Separate repo for website** - Keep `~/a327ex/Anchor/` as your main project, but have `website/` be its own git repo pushed to both GitHub and Blot

2. **Git subtree** - Single repo, push only `website/` folder to Blot using `git subtree push --prefix=website blot main`

3. **Keep Dropbox just for Blot** - Use GitHub for code, but have the website folder symlinked/copied to a Dropbox folder that Blot syncs from

---

## Key Question for the Plan

Since SessionEnd hooks won't run on accidental closure, we need a strategy for logs:

**Option A:** Write logs during the session (continuously), not just at the end. SessionEnd hook just does the final commit/push.

**Option B:** Use a PreCompact hook as a backup - it runs before context compaction, ensuring at least partial logs exist.

**Option C:** Accept that accidental closures mean you resume and manually trigger the log/commit.

Which approach sounds right to you? And for Blot - separate repo, subtree, or Dropbox?

Sources:
- [Git - Blot](https://blot.im/how/sync/git)
- [Blot GitHub repo](https://github.com/davidmerfield/blot)

## Complete Session Workflow Plan

### Project Structure

```
~/a327ex/Anchor/                    # Main project + GitHub repo
├── .git/
├── .claude/
│   └── settings.json               # Hooks configuration
├── CLAUDE.md                       # Session workflow instructions (what I read)
├── ANCHOR.md                       # Engine specification
├── IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md          # Phased checklist
├── src/                            # Engine source code
├── games/                          # Game projects
├── logs/                           # Session logs (YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md)
└── website/                        # Blot blog content
    ├── pages/
    │   └── home.md
    ├── logs/                       # Copy of session logs for blog
    └── [other blog content]
```

### What Happens Each Session

**On Start (SessionStart hook + CLAUDE.md instructions):**
1. Claude reads `CLAUDE.md` for full context
2. Creates new log file: `logs/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md`
3. Logs the session goal/task at the top

**During Session (Continuous - Option A):**
4. Claude writes to the log file as work progresses:
   - Decisions made and why
   - Code changes (what files, what changed)
   - Problems encountered and solutions
   - Any deviations from the plan
5. When any API/pattern changes: update `ANCHOR.md` and/or `CLAUDE.md` immediately
6. When implementation tasks are completed: check them off in `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md`

**On End (SessionEnd hook + CLAUDE.md instructions):**
7. Write session summary at the end of the log file
8. Copy log to `website/logs/` for the blog
9. Commit everything to git with the session summary as commit message
10. Push to GitHub (origin)
11. Push website to Blot (however we set that up)

### Handling Accidental Closure

Since logs are written continuously (Option A):
- If terminal closes unexpectedly, the log file exists with everything up to that point
- Resume with `claude --continue` or `claude --resume`
- The resumed session continues the same log file (or creates a continuation)
- SessionEnd tasks (commit, push) run when you properly end the session

### Files Claude Reads Every Session

1. **CLAUDE.md** - Contains:
   - This entire workflow (so every Claude instance knows what to do)
   - Code patterns and conventions
   - Working style preferences
   - Links to other docs

2. **ANCHOR.md** - Engine specification (read on demand, referenced from CLAUDE.md)

3. **IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md** - Current progress checklist

### Hooks Configuration

`.claude/settings.json`:
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "SessionStart": [{
      "command": "echo 'Read CLAUDE.md and start logging'"
    }],
    "SessionEnd": [{
      "command": "echo 'Summarize, commit, and push'"
    }]
  }
}
```

The hooks are reminders - the actual work is done by Claude following CLAUDE.md instructions.

---

## Remaining Decision: Blot Integration

You need to decide how to get `website/` to Blot:

**Option 1: Git Subtree** (my recommendation)
- Single repo, push website folder separately
- Command: `git subtree push --prefix=website blot main`
- Pro: Everything in one place
- Con: Subtree commands are a bit verbose

**Option 2: Separate Repo**
- `website/` is its own git repo (nested or separate location)
- Pro: Simple git push to Blot
- Con: Two repos to manage

**Option 3: Dropbox for Blot Only**
- Code on GitHub, website synced via Dropbox
- Pro: Automatic sync, no push needed
- Con: Dropbox running again

Which do you prefer for Blot?

### Phase 2: During Session (Continuous Logging)

**Step 2.1** - Claude works on the task, and after each meaningful action, updates the log:

```markdown
### 14:35 - Created spring.lua
- Added spring class with new(), update(), pull() methods
- Spring stores: name, value, target, velocity, stiffness, damping

### 14:41 - Integrated springs as child objects
- Modified object.lua to handle spring children
- Springs update automatically in parent's update cycle
- Springs die when parent dies (no manual cleanup)

### 14:48 - Problem encountered
- Spring oscillation overshooting at high stiffness values
- Solution: Clamped velocity delta per frame
```

**Step 2.2** - When Claude changes an API or establishes a new pattern, Claude immediately updates the relevant doc:

*Updates ANCHOR.md:*
```markdown
### Springs

Springs are child objects added with `+`:
\`\`\`lua
self + spring('main', 1, 200, 10)  -- name, initial, stiffness, damping
self.main:pull(0.5)                 -- pull toward 0.5
-- In draw:
game:push(x, y, 0, self.main.x, self.main.x)  -- use spring value for scale
\`\`\`
```

*Updates CLAUDE.md Patterns section:*
```markdown
### Spring Usage
\`\`\`lua
-- Add spring as child
self + spring('main', 1, 200, 10)

-- Pull spring (triggers oscillation toward target)
self.main:pull(0.5)

-- Use in drawing for juice
game:push(self.x, self.y, 0, self.main.x, self.main.x)
    game:circle(self.x, self.y, 10, color)
game:pop()
\`\`\`
```

**Step 2.3** - When a task from IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md is completed, Claude checks it off:

- [ ] Spring as child object
- [ ] pull() method
```

*After:*
```markdown
- [x] Implement spring system
- [x] Spring as child object
- [x] pull() method
```

### Phase 4: Accidental Closure (Contingency)

```

**Step 4.4** - Claude reads CLAUDE.md, sees the existing log file from today, and continues it:

```markdown
### 15:45 - Session resumed after interruption
- Continuing from previous work on springs
```

**Step 4.5** - When you're done, Phase 3 runs normally (summary, commit, push)

---

### Phase 5: Next Session (Days Later)

**Step 5.1** - You start a new session:
```bash
cd ~/a327ex/Anchor
claude
```

**Step 5.2** - Claude reads CLAUDE.md (which now contains updated patterns from last session)

**Step 5.3** - Claude reads IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md and sees checked-off tasks, knows what's done

**Step 5.4** - Claude creates a new log file: `logs/2025-01-18_10-15.md`

**Step 5.5** - The cycle repeats

> There's one mistake. I don't need an .md log file written by Claude as things are done, I also don't really need the IMPLEMENTATION PLAN or ANCHOR files changed as things are done, that can come at the end. What I need is for the entire session chat to be recorded, so it can be read later. I assume that the start session hook you're creating is doing that, right? After the session is done, Claude can then go through that file and read it to create a summary. Good catch. Let me clarify:

**Claude Code already records the full session automatically.** Transcripts are saved to `~/.claude/projects/` as JSON files. You don't need a hook to create this - it happens by default.

**The question is:** At session end, how does Claude create the summary?

**Option A: Summarize from memory (no re-read)**
- At session end, Claude still has the entire conversation in its context window (it just happened)
- Claude writes the summary from what it remembers
- No extra token cost
- This is what I'd recommend

**Option B: Re-read the transcript**
- Wasteful - the conversation is already in context
- Only needed if you resumed a compacted session and wanted to summarize the pre-compaction part too

**Option C: Write notes during session**
- What I outlined before
- Unnecessary if we just summarize from memory at the end

---

**Revised process:**

1. **During session**: Just work naturally, no logging
2. **At session end**: Claude summarizes from memory, updates docs, commits, pushes
3. **Full transcript**: Already saved by Claude Code automatically (JSON in `~/.claude/projects/`)

The only question: do you want the human-readable session log for the blog to be:
- **A summary** (what Claude writes at the end), or
- **The full conversation** (would need to convert the JSON transcript to readable markdown)

Which do you prefer?

When you resume a session, the entire conversation context is restored, including tool usage and results.\n\n## Naming Sessions\n\nGive sessions descriptive names for easier discovery later:\n\n- During a session: Use `/rename session-name` to give the conversation a memorable name\n- Later reference: Resume by name using `claude -c --resume \"auth-refactor\"`\n\n## Exporting Transcripts to Readable Formats\n\nSince the JSONL format isn't directly user-friendly, community-developed tools can convert transcripts to readable formats:\n\n### 1. **claude-code-transcripts** (Recommended)\nConverts Claude Code sessions to multi-page browseable HTML:\n- Converts `.claude/projects/` JSONL files to formatted HTML\n- Supports sharing via GitHub Gists\n- Works with both local and Claude Code on the web sessions\n\n### 2. **claude-conversation-extractor**\nInteractive tool to extract and search Claude Code history:\n- Search through conversation logs\n- Backup AI programming sessions\n- Features both TUI (Terminal UI) and CLI modes\n- Available on PyPI: `pip install claude-conversation-extractor`\n\n### 3. **claude-code-log**\nTerminal UI for browsing and managing sessions:\n- Browse Claude Code sessions with real-time navigation\n- Export selected sessions to HTML\n- Process entire `~/.claude/projects/` directory with linked index\n\n## Important Notes\n\n- Sessions are stored **locally on your machine** - Anthropic doesn't retain Claude Code session transcripts on servers beyond the configured data retention period (30 days for commercial users without opt-in)\n- The JSONL format contains complete transcript data, but it's in a programmatic format requiring parsing tools to read\n- All three export tools above are open-source community projects that parse the local JSONL files\n- The `/bug` command does send transcripts to Anthropic for bug reports, which are retained for 5 years\n\n## Permissions and Data Privacy\n\nBe aware that session files in `~/.claude/projects/` are stored locally:\n- Unencrypted on your filesystem\n- Subject to your local file permissions\n- Protected only by your OS-level security\n\nIf you're using exported transcripts, ensure you handle them securely as they contain complete conversation and code content.\n\nSources:\n- [Simon Willison's Claude Code Transcripts Tool](https://simonwillison.net/2025/Dec/25/claude-code-transcripts/)\n- [claude-code-transcripts GitHub Repository](https://github.com/simonw/claude-code-transcripts)\n- [claude-conversation-extractor GitHub](https://github.com/ZeroSumQuant/claude-conversation-extractor)\n- [claude-code-log GitHub](https://github.com/daaain/claude-code-log)\n- [Claude Code Common Workflows Documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/common-workflows.md)\n- [Claude Code Data Usage Documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/data-usage.md)"

**Location:** `~/.claude/projects/` - stored as JSONL files (JSON Lines format)

**Built-in commands:**
- `claude --continue` or `claude -c` - resume most recent session
- `claude --resume` or `claude -r` - interactive picker showing all sessions
- `/resume` during a session - same picker

**The raw files aren't human-readable** (JSONL format), but there are community tools to convert them:

1. **claude-code-transcripts** - Converts to browseable HTML
   ```bash
   pipx install claude-code-transcripts
   claude-code-transcripts    # outputs HTML
   ```

2. **claude-conversation-extractor** - Search and extract with TUI
   ```bash
   pip install claude-conversation-extractor
   ```

3. **claude-code-log** - Terminal UI browser with HTML export

Option A gives you a curated summary. Option B gives you the raw full conversation. Which fits your vision for the blog better?

## Session End - Complete Sequence

**Step 1:** You say you're done

**Step 2:** Claude locates the current session's JSONL transcript in `~/.claude/projects/`

# Session 2025-01-15 14:32

## User
Let's implement the spring system

## Claude
I'll start by reading ANCHOR.md to understand the spring specification...

[Tool: Read ANCHOR.md]

Based on the spec, springs are child objects...

## User

## Claude
Yes, I'll add a damping parameter...

[continues for entire conversation]

**Step 4:** Claude saves this to `website/logs/2025-01-15_14-32.md`

**Step 5:** Claude writes a short summary for the commit

**Step 6:** Claude updates ANCHOR.md, CLAUDE.md, IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md as needed

**Step 7:** Claude commits with the summary as the message

**Step 8:** Claude pushes to GitHub

**Step 9:** Claude subtree pushes website to Blot

- A SessionStart hook that captures the session ID and saves it to a temp file
- Or Claude searching for the most recently modified JSONL file in the project folder

Both **SessionStart** and **SessionEnd** hooks (as well as all other hooks) receive the transcript path as input.\n\n### How to Access the Transcript Path\n\nThe transcript path is available as part of the hook input JSON that Claude Code passes via stdin to your hook script. Here's what you get:\n\n**Common fields in all hook inputs:**\n\n```json\n{\n  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n  \"transcript_path\": \"/Users/.../.claude/projects/.../00893aaf-19fa-41d2-8238-13269b9b3ca0.jsonl\",\n  \"cwd\": \"/Users/...\",\n  \"permission_mode\": \"default\",\n  \"hook_event_name\": \"SessionStart\"\n}\n```\n\n**For SessionStart hooks specifically:**\n\n```json\n{\n  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n  \"transcript_path\": \"/Users/.../.claude/projects/.../00893aaf-19fa-41d2-8238-13269b9b3ca0.jsonl\",\n  \"permission_mode\": \"default\",\n  \"hook_event_name\": \"SessionStart\",\n  \"source\": \"startup\"\n}\n```\n\n**For SessionEnd hooks specifically:**\n\n```json\n{\n  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n  \"transcript_path\": \"/Users/.../.claude/projects/.../00893aaf-19fa-41d2-8238-13269b9b3ca0.jsonl\",\n  \"cwd\": \"/Users/...\",\n  \"permission_mode\": \"default\",\n  \"hook_event_name\": \"SessionEnd\",\n  \"reason\": \"exit\"\n}\n```\n\n### Key Information\n\n- **transcript_path**: The absolute path to the conversation JSON file (JSONL format)\n- **session_id**: The unique identifier for the current session\n- Both pieces of information are available in all hook events, not just SessionStart/SessionEnd\n- The transcript path is also available in environment variables during hook execution (as part of the hook input JSON via stdin)\n\n### Example Hook Usage\n\nHere's how you might use this in a SessionStart hook:\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\n# Read the hook input from stdin\ninput=$(cat)\nsession_id=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.session_id')\ntranscript_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.transcript_path')\n\necho \"Session ID: $session_id\"\necho \"Transcript path: $transcript_path\"\n\nexit 0\n```\n\nFor more details, see the [hooks documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks.md#hook-input)."

# Chat Log Format Analysis

Based on the content provided, here's the chat structure:

## Message Formatting

**User Messages:**
- Introduced with `> # Task [number]: [title]`
- Multi-line text content follows
- Code examples embedded with backticks or indentation
- Clear topic delineation with headers

**Assistant/Claude Messages:**
- Prefixed with `⏺` symbol for actions/tool usage
- Structured as nested operations with indentation
- Tool results marked with `⎿` for sub-items
- Output sections show file reads/writes with line counts

## Key Separators

- `∴ Thinking…` marks internal reasoning blocks
- `⏺ [Action]` indicates Claude performing tasks
- `⎿ [Result]` shows operation outcomes
- `[content truncated]` indicates clipped output

## Structure Pattern

```
> # [User Prompt]
[Content]
... [10 more lines]
```

**Key finding for the plan:** The JSONL transcript contains all the data needed to reconstruct this format:
- `type: "user"` → `>` prefix
- `type: "assistant"` with `tool_use` → `⏺ ToolName (args)`

- `type: "assistant"` with `text` → plain text

```
Let me check your current Hyprland configuration to see how it's set up:
Let me also check the default windows config to see existing patterns:
Based on your Hyprland config, here are both options:

## Option 1: Separate Workspace (Recommended - Much Easier)

Add this to the bottom of your `~/.config/hypr/hyprland.conf`:

```
# Discord on workspace 10
windowrule = workspace 10, class:discord
```

This will always send Discord to workspace 10. You can switch there with `Super+0`.

## Option 2: Background on Workspace 1 (Complex)

True "background" behavior is tricky in Hyprland since windows don't have z-order layers like traditional desktops. You could try:

```
# Discord fullscreen on workspace 1
windowrule = workspace 1, class:discord
windowrule = fullscreen, class:discord
```

But the problem is: other windows on workspace 1 would be **behind** fullscreen Discord, not in front of it. There's no native way to pin a window to the background layer.

---

**My recommendation**: Use the separate workspace approach. It's cleaner and you can quickly peek at Discord with `Super+0`, then return with `Super+1`. You could also use a scratchpad/special workspace if you want Discord to overlay temporarily.
```

> OK, what's the easiest way to view a Markdown file as it will look on the web?

A few options:

**1. glow (terminal)** - Renders markdown nicely in terminal
```bash
yay -S glow
glow ~/a327ex/session-sample.md
```

**2. Browser preview** - Open GitHub/GitLab and paste it, or use a local tool:
```bash
yay -S pandoc
pandoc ~/a327ex/session-sample.md -o /tmp/preview.html && xdg-open /tmp/preview.html
```

> There are some weird line breaks in some messages, like "and how to configure /// specific" or "Please tell me about /// any", do you know why?

That's from me manually adding line breaks when I wrote the sample file. When generating the real transcript from JSONL, the text should stay on one line (or wrap naturally by the viewer).

For example, I wrote:
```
  ⎿ Find information about window rules, workspace assignment, and how to configure
    specific applications...
```

But it should be:
```
  ⎿ Find information about window rules, workspace assignment, and how to configure specific applications...
```

The conversion script should preserve the original text without adding manual breaks. Glow will wrap it properly based on your terminal width.

```
# Installing markdown-preview.nvim with lazy.nvim

Based on the documentation, there are two installation approaches:

## Without Node/Yarn/NPM

```lua
{
  "iamcco/markdown-preview.nvim",
  cmd = { "MarkdownPreviewToggle", "MarkdownPreview", "MarkdownPreviewStop" },
  ft = { "markdown" },
  build = function() vim.fn["mkdp#util#install"]() end,
}
```

## With Node/Yarn/NPM

```lua
{
  "iamcco/markdown-preview.nvim",
  cmd = { "MarkdownPreviewToggle", "MarkdownPreview", "MarkdownPreviewStop" },
  build = "cd app && yarn install",
  init = function()
    vim.g.mkdp_filetypes = { "markdown" }
  end,
  ft = { "markdown" },
}
```

The key difference is the `build` command: use `vim.fn["mkdp#util#install"]()` for the pre-built version, or `"cd app && yarn install"` if you have Node.js/Yarn installed. The second approach also includes an `init` function to configure the plugin's filetypes.
```

The first approach I used was correct according to docs. The issue might be timing - the plugin wasn't loaded when build ran. Let me try the yarn/npm approach:

## Complete Plan (Merged & Updated)

### Project Structure

```
/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/              ← Git repo (github.com/a327ex/anchor)
├── .claude/
│   ├── settings.json                 ← Hook configuration
│   └── session-timestamps.log        ← Backup timestamps
├── .gitignore
├── CLAUDE.md                         ← Master instructions for all Claude instances
├── ANCHOR.md                         ← Engine specification
├── IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md            ← Phased checklist
├── src/                              ← C source (future)
├── yue/                              ← YueScript source (future)
├── lua/                              ← Compiled Lua output (future)
├── assets/                           ← Game assets (future)
├── scripts/
│   └── jsonl-to-markdown.py          ← Transcript converter
└── website/                          ← Blot website (subtree pushed to Blot)
    ├── logs/                         ← Full session transcripts (Markdown)
    ├── pages/                        ← Website pages
    ├── context/                      ← Copies of ANCHOR.md, CLAUDE.md, IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md
    ├── files/                        ← Downloadable files (.yue examples, etc.)
    └── notes/                        ← Notes and blog posts
```

---

### Git Remotes

```
origin  → git@github.com:a327ex/anchor.git     (main repo)
blot    → https://blot.im/git/[your-url]       (website only, via subtree)
```

---

### What Gets Logged

1. **Full transcript** → `website/logs/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md`
   - The entire conversation in readable Markdown format
   - Generated by `scripts/jsonl-to-markdown.py` from Claude Code's JSONL transcript
   - Preserves the terminal-style format (⏺ for tools, ⎿ for results, > for user)

2. **Summary** → Git commit message
   - Short description of what was accomplished
   - Used as the commit message

---

### Session Lifecycle - Complete Step-by-Step

#### Phase 1: Session Start

**Step 1.1** - You open terminal and run:
```bash
cd ~/a327ex/Anchor
claude
```

**Step 1.2** - SessionStart hook fires, logs timestamp to `.claude/session-timestamps.log`

**Step 1.3** - Claude reads `CLAUDE.md` automatically (Claude Code does this for any CLAUDE.md in working directory)

**Step 1.4** - You state what you want to work on

---

#### Phase 2: During Session

**Step 2.1** - Work proceeds normally. No manual logging needed - Claude Code automatically saves the full transcript to `~/.claude/projects/[path]/[session-id].jsonl`

**Step 2.2** - When Claude changes an API or establishes a new pattern, Claude updates:
- `ANCHOR.md` for API/architecture changes
- `CLAUDE.md` for patterns/conventions
- `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` for completed tasks

---

#### Phase 3: Session End

**Step 3.1** - You say "let's wrap up" (or similar)

**Step 3.2** - Claude locates the current session's JSONL transcript (path provided by hook or found via most recent file)

**Step 3.3** - Claude runs the converter:
```bash
python3 scripts/jsonl-to-markdown.py ~/.claude/projects/[...]/[session].jsonl website/logs/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md
```

**Step 3.4** - Claude writes a short summary of what was accomplished

**Step 3.5** - Claude syncs context files:
```bash
cp ANCHOR.md website/context/
cp CLAUDE.md website/context/
cp IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md website/context/
```

**Step 3.6** - Claude stages all changes:
```bash
git add -A
```

**Step 3.7** - Claude commits with summary:
```bash
git commit -m "Summary of session

- Bullet point 1
- Bullet point 2

🤖 Generated with Claude Code"
```

**Step 3.8** - Claude pushes to GitHub:
```bash
git push origin main
```

**Step 3.9** - Claude pushes website to Blot:
```bash
git subtree push --prefix=website blot main
```

**Step 3.10** - Claude confirms:
```
Session complete.
- Transcript saved: website/logs/2025-01-15_14-32.md
- Committed to GitHub: [hash]
- Website pushed to Blot
```

**Step 3.11** - SessionEnd hook fires, logs timestamp

---

#### Phase 4: Accidental Closure

**Step 4.1** - Terminal closes unexpectedly

**Step 4.2** - The JSONL transcript exists with everything up to that point (Claude Code saves continuously)

**Step 4.3** - You reopen and resume:
```bash
cd ~/a327ex/Anchor
claude --continue
```

**Step 4.4** - Claude has full context. Ask "where were we?" if needed.

**Step 4.5** - When ready to end, Phase 3 runs normally - transcript includes both parts of the session

---

#### Phase 5: Next Session

**Step 5.1** - Start new session:
```bash
cd ~/a327ex/Anchor
claude
```

**Step 5.2** - Claude reads updated `CLAUDE.md`, `ANCHOR.md`, `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md`

**Step 5.3** - Previous session's log is on the website for reference

**Step 5.4** - Cycle repeats

---

### Hook Configuration (`.claude/settings.json`)

```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "SessionStart": [
      {
        "matcher": "startup|resume",
        "hooks": [
          {
            "type": "command",
            "command": "echo \"[$(date '+%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')] Session started\" >> /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/session-timestamps.log"
          }
        ]
      }
    ],
    "SessionEnd": [
      {
        "hooks": [
          {
            "type": "command",
            "command": "echo \"[$(date '+%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')] Session ended\" >> /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/session-timestamps.log"
          }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

\`\`\`

> Next user message

...

> Great, now let's work on the bigger plan itself. Let me read the file you created. What is session-timestamps.log for?

The `session-timestamps.log` is a backup mechanism. The hooks automatically log when sessions start and end:

```
[2025-01-15 14:32:00] Session started
[2025-01-15 16:45:12] Session ended
```

**Why it exists:** If you accidentally close the terminal (Phase 4 in the plan), the SessionEnd hook never fires, so the end-of-session ritual (convert transcript, commit, push) doesn't happen. The timestamp log gives you a record that a session happened, even if it wasn't properly closed.

**In practice:** It's just a safety net. The real transcript is in Claude Code's JSONL files. The timestamps help you:
1. Know when sessions occurred
2. Correlate with JSONL files if you need to manually recover
3. Detect sessions that weren't properly ended (no "Session ended" entry)

If you don't think you need it, we can remove it from the plan - the JSONL transcripts are the real source of truth anyway.

> The git repo for the blog is https://blot.im/clients/git/end/anchor.git, you may change the file with that information. I don't know what we need to do to actually interact with it how we intend to, though.

Updated. Here's how the Blot interaction works:

**Setup (one-time):**
```bash
cd ~/a327ex/Anchor
git remote add blot https://blot.im/clients/git/end/anchor.git
```

**Pushing website to Blot:**
```bash
git subtree push --prefix=website blot main
```

This takes only the `website/` folder and pushes it to Blot as if it were the root of a repo. Blot sees:
```
logs/
pages/
context/
files/
notes/
```

Not the full Anchor project structure.

**First push might need:**
```bash
git subtree push --prefix=website blot main --force
```

**Credentials:** Blot will ask for username/password on first push. The URL suggests it uses HTTP auth - you likely set a password when configuring Git sync in Blot's dashboard.

**The flow:**
1. You work in `~/a327ex/Anchor/`
2. Website content lives in `website/` subfolder
3. `git push origin main` → pushes everything to GitHub
4. `git subtree push --prefix=website blot main` → pushes only `website/` to Blot
5. Blot rebuilds your site from that content

Want me to test if the Blot remote is accessible, or wait until we set up the full project structure?

> One change, please change the SESSION_WORKFLOW document to include that, the summary that is also used as a commit message is also pasted at the top of the log file, before the chat conversation log happens. This way, to see a summary of the conversation, you can just read the start of the file. This means that your steps in phase 3 are a bit out of order. Or maybe not out of order, but you have to write the summary *and* add it to the top of log file.

You're missing the gstreamer plugin packages (only have the libs). Try:

```bash
yay -S gst-plugins-good gst-plugins-bad gst-plugins-ugly gst-libav
```

If that doesn't fix it, the green video is often a Chrome + Nvidia hardware acceleration issue. You can try disabling hardware acceleration in Chrome:
1. Go to `chrome://settings/system`
2. Turn off "Use graphics acceleration when available"

Or try with these Chrome flags in `chrome://flags`:
- Set "Hardware-accelerated video decode" to Disabled

Let me know if installing the gstreamer plugins helps first.

> It was the hardware acceleration. Does that make it slower to play videos or what?

With hardware acceleration **disabled**:
- **CPU decodes video** instead of GPU
- Uses more CPU, more battery (on laptops)
- GPU sits idle during video playback

With hardware acceleration **enabled**:
- **GPU decodes video** (dedicated hardware)
- Almost no CPU usage
- More power efficient

For typical browsing/4chan webms, you won't notice a difference - modern CPUs handle it easily. It matters more for:
- 4K video
- Multiple videos at once
- Laptops on battery

The green/buggy video is a known Chrome + Nvidia + Linux issue with VA-API. You could try to fix it properly later by tweaking `libva-nvidia-driver` settings, but disabling acceleration is the quick fix that just works.

> I'd like to fix it properly, I watch streams a lot and it seems like having that on CPU would be a mistake.

Web search results for query: "Chrome Nvidia Linux VA-API green video fix libva-nvidia-driver 2024 2025"

Links: [{"title":"Chrome Support · Issue #5 · elFarto/nvidia-vaapi-driver","url":"https://github.com/elFarto/nvidia-vaapi-driver/issues/5"},{"title":"NVIDIA VA-API Driver 0.0.12 Brings Fixes, Chrome Compatibility Work - Phoronix","url":"https://www.phoronix.com/news/NVIDIA-VA-API-Driver-0.0.12"},{"title":"GitHub - elFarto/nvidia-vaapi-driver: A VA-API implemention using NVIDIA's NVDEC","url":"https://github.com/elFarto/nvidia-vaapi-driver"},{"title":"chromium: hardware video acceleration with VA-API (Page 47) / Applications & Desktop Environments / Arch Linux Forums","url":"https://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=244031&p=47"},{"title":"libva Configuration for hybrid Intel/NVIDIA: conflicting chrome/vainfo / Laptop Issues / Arch Linux Forums","url":"https://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=292650"},{"title":"HardwareVideoAcceleration - Debian Wiki","url":"https://wiki.debian.org/HardwareVideoAcceleration"},{"title":"Lack of VA-API Support – GPU Video Decode Issue in Chromium-Based Browsers - Linux - NVIDIA Developer Forums","url":"https://forums.developer.nvidia.com/t/lack-of-va-api-support-gpu-video-decode-issue-in-chromium-based-browsers/351059"},{"title":"Hardware video acceleration - ArchWiki","url":"https://wiki.archlinux.org/title/Hardware_video_acceleration"},{"title":"Proper VA-API support - Linux - NVIDIA Developer Forums","url":"https://forums.developer.nvidia.com/t/proper-va-api-support/305066"},{"title":"Chromium Docs - VA-API","url":"https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/lkgr/docs/gpu/vaapi.md"}]

Based on the search results, here's what I found about Chrome, NVIDIA, VA-API, and the libva-nvidia-driver:

## Current Status

Chrome is currently unsupported, and will not function according to the official nvidia-vaapi-driver GitHub repository.

## Recent Development Progress

The nvidia-vaapi-driver 0.0.12 release (May 2024) adds single buffer export support for working on Chrome/Chromium browser support along with increasing the number of render targets to 32.(no content)This update is mostly a small set of bug fixes but does contain some work for enabling some support for the Chrome/Chromium web browser.

## Ongoing Issues (2025)

Users on Arch Linux forums report ongoing problems. Chrome remains unusable in native Wayland mode.(no content)Despite Video Acceleration Information table in chrome://gpu was filled with codec information, videos were not accelerated.(no content)Especially in Chromium-based browsers (Chrome, Edge, Thorium), the GPU video decode chain runs via the VA-API. However, because the NVIDIA driver doesn't officially support the VA-API, video decode operations fall to the CPU, severely impacting system performance.

## Configuration Tips

For NVIDIA NVDEC use nvidia as the `LIBVA_DRIVER_NAME` environment variable.

VA-API support is enabled by default in Chromium. It has been reported that some may need to specify --enable-features=VaapiVideoDecodeLinuxGL to let Chromium actually detect formats the hardware could accelerate.(no content)Requires NVIDIA driver >= 580.105.08 for certain power management features in newer versions.

## Verification

To verify that the build and platform supports video acceleration, launch Chromium and navigate to chrome://gpu, then: Search for the "Video Acceleration Information" Section: this should enumerate the available accelerated codecs and resolutions.

The search results didn't specifically mention a "green video" fix, but the underlying issue appears to be that Chrome/Chromium support with nvidia-vaapi-driver is still a work in progress and not fully functional.

⏺ WebFetch (https://github.com/elFarto/nvidia-vaapi-driver)  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;⎿ Result:

```
# Chrome/Chromium Support Status

## Current Status
According to the documentation, **"Chrome is currently unsupported, and will not function."** There is no active development or roadmap for Chrome compatibility.

## Environment Variables & Configuration
Since Chrome support doesn't exist, no specific environment variables or configuration recommendations are provided for it. The driver is designed primarily for Firefox.

## Green/Corrupt Video Issues
The documentation doesn't address green or corrupt video problems for Chrome (or any browser). However, it does mention that the EGL backend is broken on NVIDIA driver versions 525+, recommending users switch to the direct backend instead via the `NVD_BACKEND=direct` environment variable.

## Requirements
General requirements for the driver include:
- NVIDIA driver series 470 or 500+
- The `nvidia_drm` kernel module configured with `nvidia-drm.modeset=1`

For functional video decoding, you also need ffmpeg compiled with VA-API support.

**Bottom line:** Chrome simply isn't supported by this VA-API driver implementation.
```

Bad news: **Chrome is officially unsupported** by the nvidia-vaapi-driver. The project explicitly states it won't work with Chrome.

Your options:

- Hardware acceleration actually works
- Could use Firefox for streams, Chrome for everything else

- CPU decoding works fine
- For streams, your CPU can handle it (what CPU do you have?)

**Option 3: Try experimental Chrome flags** (might not work)

- Enable "Vulkan"
```
Then re-enable hardware acceleration and test

# Initial commit (no auth needed)

git commit -m "Initial commit - project structure and documentation"

# Pull Blot content into website/ (will ask for Blot password)
git subtree add --prefix=website blot main

# Push to GitHub (uses SSH key, should work)
git push -u origin main
```

Run these in your terminal. The `subtree add` command will prompt for your Blot credentials.

> Anchor master ✗ git subtree add --prefix=website blot main

fatal: couldn't find remote ref main

Blot might use `master` instead of `main`:

```bash
git subtree add --prefix=website blot master
```

Or check what branches exist:

```bash
git ls-remote blot
```

> Great, master worked. Just to show you what website contains: Anchor master ❯ ls website
Permissions Size User Date Modified Name
drwxr-xr-x     - adn   1 Jan 06:01   context
drwxr-xr-x     - adn   1 Jan 06:01   files
drwxr-xr-x     - adn   1 Jan 06:01   notes

It doesn't contain the logs folder yet because there are no logs. But we'll add that later, I assume. So now I should just git push -u origin main? Why does it say "Anchor master" on my terminal?

The terminal says "master" because git created a `master` branch by default (older git behavior). GitHub expects `main`.

Rename the branch first, then push:

```bash
git branch -M main
git push -u origin main
```

The `-M` renames `master` to `main`. Then it should work with GitHub.

And yes, the `logs/` folder will be created when we save the first session log.

> OK, now, how do we keep the main folder from having lots of MD files thrown around everywhere? Currently there are 4, but that will likely grow. Can't we create a folder for that that CLAUDE can read from? Or does it only read files automatically if they're in the folder where you started the session from?

⏺ Task (Check CLAUDE.md location rules)  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;⎿ Result:

```
[
  {
    "type": "text",
    "text": "Perfect! I have the information you need. Here's what the documentation says about CLAUDE.md file location and automatic reading:\n\n## CLAUDE.md File Location Rules\n\nClaude Code does NOT only read CLAUDE.md from the root directory. Instead, it uses a **recursive, hierarchical approach**:\n\n### Key Rules:\n\n1. **Upward recursion from your working directory**: Claude Code reads memories recursively starting in your current working directory (cwd) and recurses **up** to (but not including) the root directory `/`. Any `CLAUDE.md` or `CLAUDE.local.md` files found are automatically loaded.\n\n2. **Downward discovery in subtrees**: Claude also discovers CLAUDE.md files nested in **subtrees** under your current working directory. However, these are loaded lazily\u2014only when Claude reads files in those subtrees, not at launch.\n\n3. **Multiple valid locations**:\n   - `./CLAUDE.md` - Project memory at root\n   - `./.claude/CLAUDE.md` - Project memory in `.claude` directory\n   - `./CLAUDE.local.md` - Personal project-specific preferences (automatically added to .gitignore)\n   - `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` - User memory (applies to all projects)\n   - `./.claude/rules/*.md` - Modular project rules\n\n### Example Scenario:\n\nIf you run Claude Code in `foo/bar/` and have CLAUDE.md files in both `foo/CLAUDE.md` and `foo/bar/CLAUDE.md`, **both will be automatically loaded**. The hierarchy means more specific (lower level) memories take precedence.\n\n### Precedence Order (highest to lowest):\n\n1. Enterprise policy (system-level)\n2. Project memory (`./CLAUDE.md` or `./.claude/CLAUDE.md`)\n3. Project rules (`./.claude/rules/*.md`)\n4. User memory (`~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`)\n5. Project local memory (`./CLAUDE.local.md`)\n\n## Key Takeaway:\n\nYou can absolutely have CLAUDE.md in subfolders and they will be automatically read. Claude's memory system is designed to support nested directory structures, making it convenient for large repositories where you work in subdirectories.\n\n**To view what memory files are actually loaded**, use:\n```\n/memory\n```\n\nThis command shows you all loaded memory files in your current session, which is helpful for debugging which files are being included."
  },
  {
    "type": "text",
    "text": "agentId: abd2911 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)"
  }
]
```

Good news - you can put CLAUDE.md in `.claude/CLAUDE.md` and it will still be read automatically.

For the others, we could do:

```
/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/
├── .claude/
│   ├── CLAUDE.md          ← Auto-read
│   ├── settings.json
│   └── docs/

```
├── .claude/

Analysis:
Let me chronologically analyze this conversation:

1. **Initial Context**: This is a continuation of a previous session that was compacted. The user is setting up their Omarchy system (Arch Linux + Hyprland) for game development using Claude Code. The main project is **Anchor** - a C/YueScript game engine.

2. **Dropbox Removal**: User returned after reboot, Dropbox was still running. I removed Dropbox folders and uninstalled the package. Updated Ghostty scroll speed to 3.5.

3. **Session Workflow Planning**: The user wanted to set up a comprehensive session workflow:
   - Every session saved and logged automatically
   - Documentation files auto-updated (ANCHOR.md, CLAUDE.md, IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md)
   - Full transcript + summary logged to website
   - Commits to GitHub with summary as message
   - Website pushed to Blot via git subtree

4. **Session Persistence Research**: Found that Claude Code sessions are saved automatically to `~/.claude/projects/` as JSONL files. Sessions can be resumed with `claude --continue`. The hooks provide `transcript_path` in their input.

5. **Blot Research**: Discovered Blot doesn't support subdirectories - need to use git subtree to push only `website/` folder.

6. **JSONL to Markdown Converter**: Created `jsonl-to-markdown.py` script to convert Claude Code transcripts to readable Markdown format with terminal-style symbols (⏺, ⎿, >).

7. **Markdown Preview**: Installed markdown-preview.nvim for NeoVim. Had build issues, fixed by using npm approach.

8. **Formatting Fixes**: User wanted proper line breaks and indentation for the ⎿ symbol. Fixed by using `&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;` (3 non-breaking spaces) for indentation.

9. **Plan Documentation**: Saved the complete workflow plan to `SESSION_WORKFLOW_PLAN.md`.

10. **Chrome Video Fix**: User had green/buggy webm videos. Fixed by installing `intel-media-driver` and setting Chrome to use Intel VA-API instead of Nvidia.

11. **Project Setup**: Created the Anchor project structure, initialized git, set up remotes for GitHub and Blot, used git subtree to pull existing Blot content.

12. **File Reorganization**: Moved CLAUDE.md to `.claude/CLAUDE.md` and created `docs/` folder for ANCHOR.md, IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md, SESSION_WORKFLOW_PLAN.md. Updated references in CLAUDE.md.

Key errors and fixes:
- JSONL parsing: result was sometimes a list, not string - fixed by checking type before string operations
- Markdown line breaks: needed two spaces before newline for proper breaks
- Indentation stripped: used `&nbsp;` HTML entities instead of regular spaces
- Git branch naming: Blot uses `master`, GitHub uses `main` - had to rename branch and use correct branch names
- Chrome VA-API: Nvidia not supported, used Intel iGPU instead

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **JSONL parsing AttributeError**: `result.split('\n')` failed when result was a list
     - Fix: Check `isinstance(result, list)` before string operations
   - **Markdown line breaks not working**: Single `\n` doesn't create line break in Markdown
     - Fix: Add two spaces before newline: `f"⏺ {tool_name} {formatted_input}  \n"`
   - **⎿ indentation stripped**: Regular spaces stripped by Markdown renderer
     - Fix: Use `&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;` HTML entities instead
     - User feedback: "Almost. It's on a new line, but the symbol is still not aligned" → "I think it needs 2 more spaces" → "Actually, it was 3"
   - **Git branch mismatch**: Blot uses `master`, created repo defaulted to `master`
     - Fix: `git branch -M main` to rename for GitHub
   - **Chrome green/buggy video**: Nvidia VA-API not supported in Chrome
     - Fix: Install `intel-media-driver`, set `LIBVA_DRIVER_NAME=iHD` for Chrome
   - **markdown-preview.nvim build failed**: `mkdp#util#install` unknown function
     - Fix: Use `build = "cd app && npm install"` instead

> Alright, great. Is there a way to setup the engine as a public repository (like it is now), but the games made with it as private, while inside the Anchor folder? Or will I need a new repo for each game if I want it to be private?

Yes, you can nest git repos. The simplest approach:

1. Create a `games/` folder in Anchor
2. Add `games/` to Anchor's `.gitignore`
3. Each game inside (`games/emoji-ball-battles/`) is its own git repo pointing to a private GitHub repo

```
Anchor/                          ← public repo
├── .gitignore                   ← contains "games/"
├── src/
├── yue/
└── games/                       ← ignored by Anchor repo
    └── emoji-ball-battles/      ← separate private repo
        ├── .git/
        ├── main.yue
        └── ...
```

The game folder lives inside Anchor on disk but is completely separate in git. No submodules, no complexity.

The game repo can reference engine files via relative paths (`../../src/`, `../../yue/`) since they're siblings on disk.

Want me to set this up?

> Yes, additionally move the example .yue files to the Anchor/yue folder.

⏺ Glob (**/*.yue)

> Are those commands going to be available to all Claude instances from now on? Where were they saved? What do they look like internally?

To be honest - they're not real Claude Code slash commands. They're just instructions in CLAUDE.md that I'll interpret.

What I did was add text that says:
```markdown
**`/end`** → run the full workflow below
**`/end-no-save`** → just end the session
```

Any Claude instance that reads CLAUDE.md (which happens automatically when starting from the Anchor folder) will see this and follow it. But it's just a documented convention, not a registered command in Claude Code's system.

Real slash commands (skills) would need to be configured separately. Want me to look into setting up actual Claude Code skills for these? Or is the CLAUDE.md convention sufficient?

> I don't know, you tell me if it's sufficient, I don't know how Claude Code works entirely yet.

The CLAUDE.md convention is sufficient. Here's why:

Claude Code is designed to read and follow CLAUDE.md instructions - that's the whole point of the file. When I see `/end`, I'll recognize it as the instruction to run the workflow. It's unambiguous and reliable.

Real skills would only add value if:
- You wanted tab-completion for commands
- The command needed to trigger external scripts Claude can't run
- You wanted it to work without reading CLAUDE.md first

None of those apply here. The documented convention will work fine.

> Great, another question, is the CLAUDE.md file too big with redundant information? I was thinking that maybe a lot of the patterns should just be kept in ANCHOR.md, but I'm not sure, I'd have to test if that changes how good you are at generating code in a way I approve.

Honest assessment: there's some conceptual overlap, but the current split makes sense:

**CLAUDE.md** = *how to work* (workflow, style, decision points, common mistakes)

**ANCHOR.md** = *what the engine is* (architecture, APIs, technical spec)

The patterns in CLAUDE.md are more "how to write code in this style" - they're instructions for me. ANCHOR.md is the reference spec.

That said, I haven't read ANCHOR.md this session, so I can't compare them in detail. The real test is whether I generate code you approve of. If I'm making mistakes that better documentation would fix, we adjust.

Size isn't a problem for my context - it's more about clarity. I'd suggest leaving it as-is until you see actual problems with my code output, then we can reorganize based on what's going wrong.
